(NYSE:NKE) today reported fiscal 2020 financial results for its </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">third quarter</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;ended </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">February&#160;29, 2020</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Revenues rose </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">5 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a reported basis and </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis*; Digital sales up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">36 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;versus prior year</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Diluted earnings per share was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$0.53</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, including a </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$0.25</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;non-recurring, non-cash charge associated with the transition to a strategic distributor model in South America</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Inventory increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$5.8 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">; closeout inventory units declined versus prior year</font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Revenues increased to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$10.1 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;in the </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">third quarter</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">5 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a reported basis and up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis, driven by </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">13 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;currency-neutral growth in NIKE Direct with digital growth of </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">36 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;and strong growth across EMEA, APLA and North America, offset by the impact of COVID-19 on our business in Greater China. Digital sales in Greater China increased more than </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">30 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;while brick and mortar retail sales were impacted by temporary store closures related to COVID-19.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;In an extraordinarily dynamic time, NIKE&#8217;s strong results are testament to our deep consumer connections, compelling product innovation and agile teams around the world. We know it&#8217;s in times like these that strong brands get even stronger,&#8221; said John Donahoe, President and CEO, NIKE, Inc. &#8220;As we start to see recovery in China, no one is better equipped than NIKE to navigate the current climate.&#8221;**</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Diluted earnings per share for the quarter was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$0.53</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, including a </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$0.25</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;non-recurring, non-cash charge related to our entry into definitive agreements to transition our Brazil, Argentina, Chile and Uruguay businesses to a strategic distributor model. Diluted earnings per share was also adversely impacted by COVID-19.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;As we close Q3, NIKE&#8217;s Brand leadership and business momentum have been stronger than ever and unrivaled around the world,&#8221; said Andy Campion, Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer, NIKE, Inc. &#8220;Amidst the dynamics that all are facing, we are executing against an operational playbook that will expedite NIKE&#8217;s return to profitable, capital efficient growth leveraging our strong financial position, the strongest partnerships across the value chain in our industry, and our leading digital capabilities.&#8221;**</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">COVID-19 Update</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">As discussed in our press release issued on February 4, 2020, operations in Greater China were materially impacted as a result of COVID-19. In the third quarter, on a currency-neutral basis, Greater China revenues were down </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">4 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;following </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">22</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;consecutive quarters of double-digit growth. However, during the first two months of the third quarter, Greater China&#8217;s revenue grew strong double digits, offset by the impacts of COVID-19 beginning in late January. At the peak in February, roughly </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">75 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;of NIKE-owned and partner doors in Greater China were closed with others operating on reduced hours. Currently, nearly </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">80 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;of doors are open in Greater China with an even higher rate in key cities. Beginning March 16</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:7pt">th</sup></font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, all NIKE-owned stores, outside of Greater China, Japan and Korea were closed to help curb the spread of COVID-19.  </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">NIKE, Inc. management will provide more detail on the financial and operational impacts of COVID-19 during the conference call later today.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">Non-recurring Items Impacting Comparability in the Third Quarter</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Third quarter results contain several non-comparable transactions. In February, we announced the execution of agreements to transition our NIKE Brand businesses in Brazil, Argentina, Chile and Uruguay to strategic distributor partnerships. As a result, we classified the assets and liabilities of the entities to be sold as held-for-sale on our Unaudited Consolidated Balance Sheets and recognized a non-recurring, non-cash charge of </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$400 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">. This charge primarily reflects the anticipated release of associated cumulative foreign currency translation losses and could fluctuate due to changes in exchange rates up to the date of close. Additionally, we completed the sale of the Hurley brand and recognized an immaterial gain on sale. Both the Hurley gain on sale and the charge associated with the transition in South America were recognized in Other (income) expense, net on our Unaudited Consolidated Statements of Income. As a result of the sale of the Hurley business, the Company estimates that revenue growth in North America was adversely impacted by approximately </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">1-2</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;percentage points during the third quarter. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">Third Quarter</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;Income Statement Review</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Revenues</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">for NIKE, Inc. increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">5 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$10.1 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#9702;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Revenues for the NIKE Brand were </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$9.6 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">6 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis driven by double-digit growth in NIKE Direct and growth in wholesale; key categories including Sportswear and the Jordan Brand, and continued growth across footwear and apparel.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#9702;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Revenues for Converse were $</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">506 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">11 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis, mainly driven by double-digit growth in Europe and in digital, globally. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Gross margin</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">80 basis points</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">44.3 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;primarily as a result of impacts from COVID-19, including a lower mix of sales in Greater China which is our highest margin geography, as well as increased rebates to wholesale partners and higher costs related to factory cancellations to manage future inventory. Gross margin also declined due to changes in foreign exchange rates and incremental tariffs in North America. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Selling and administrative expense</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">6 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$3.3 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">. Demand creation expense was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$870 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">1 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;due primarily to investments in key brand moments. Operating overhead expense increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">8 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$2.4 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;driven by wage-related expenses, which reflect investments in data and analytics and other transformational initiatives to accelerate our end-to-end digital transformation. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Other (income) expense, net</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$297 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;comprised primarily of a non-recurring, non-cash charge of </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$400 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;related to the execution of agreements to transition the Company&#8217;s operating models in Brazil, Argentina, Chile and Uruguay. This charge largely reflects the anticipated release of associated cumulative foreign currency translation losses.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div if(e)e.style.display='block';Show.LastAR=e};Show.hideAR=function(){Show.LastAR.style.display='none'};Show.toggleNext=function(a){var e=a;while(e.nodeName!='DIV')e=e.nextSibling;if(!e.style){}else if(!e.style.display){}else{var d,p_;if(e.style.display=='none'){d='block';p='-'}else{d='none';p='+'}
